## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship of a material. Temperature typically softens materials (reducing flow stress), while strain typically hardens them, and classical constitutive models capture these competing effects through power-law hardening and thermal softening terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent elastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (elastic modulus with Arrhenius-type temperature dependence)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon model)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress)
- Johnson-Cook (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook homologous: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - ((T - c3) * c4)**c5) (power-law thermal softening with homologous temperature)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 / T) (Zener-Hollomon type at constant strain rate)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal softening)
- Polynomial with thermal coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (quadratic with cross terms)
- Exponential softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**c3 * exp(c4 * T) (nonlinear elastoplastic with temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * log(c1 * exp(c2 / T) + c3 * epsilon**c4) (thermally activated flow)
- Rational thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (1 + c2 * T**c3) (hardening with rational temperature dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (work hardening) → Power-law form epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturation form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening of flow stress → Multiplicative factor that decreases with T: exp(-c*T), (1 - c*T**m), or 1/(1+c*T)
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius-type term exp(c/T) reflecting activation energy barriers
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield before hardening: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Multiplicative decomposition of effects → Stress as product of separate strain and temperature functions: sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T)
- Voce-type saturation hardening → Form (c0 - c1*exp(-c2*epsilon)) where stress saturates at large strains
- Hyperbolic sine stress dependence → sinh(c*sigma) appears in creep/flow models linking to Arrhenius kinetics
- Phase transition or anomalous softening → Non-monotonic temperature dependence suggesting piecewise or Gaussian bump in T
